save the <i><a href="/wiki/Mail_%26_Guardian" title="Mail &amp; Guardian">Mail &amp; Guardian</a></i> in South Africa. However, GMG sold the majority of its shares of the <i>Mail &amp; Guardian</i> in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>The Guardian</i> was consistently loss-making until 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> The National Newspaper division of GMG, which also includes <i>The Observer</i>, reported operating losses of \xc2\xa349.9 million in 2006, up from \xc2\xa318.6 million in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The paper was therefore heavily dependent on cross-subsidisation from profitable companies within the group.\n</p><p>The continual losses made by the National Newspaper division of the <i>Guardian Media Group</i> caused it to dispose of its Regional Media division by selling titles to competitor <i><a href="/wiki/Trinity_Mirror" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinity Mirror">Trinity Mirror</a></i> in March 2010. This included the flagship <i><a href="/wiki/Manchester_Evening_News" title="Manchester Evening News">Manchester Evening News</a></i>, and severed the historic link between that paper and <i>The Guardian</i>. The sale was in order to safeguard the future of <i>The Guardian</i> newspaper as is the intended purpose of the <i>Scott Trust</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-M.E.N_sold_to_Trinity_Mirror_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-M.E.N_sold_to_Trinity_Mirror-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2011 <i>Guardian News and Media</i> revealed increased annual losses of \xc2\xa333 million and announced that it was looking to focus on its online edition for news coverage, leaving the print edition to contain more comments and features. It was also speculated that <i>The Guardian</i> might become the first British national daily paper to be fully online.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For the three years up to June 2012, the paper lost \xc2\xa3100,000 a day, which prompted <i>Intelligent Life</i> to question whether <i>The Guardian</i> could survive.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 2007 and 2014 <i>The Guardian Media Group</i> sold all their side businesses, of regional papers and online portals for classifieds and consolidated, into <i>The Guardian</i> as sole product. The sales let them acquire a capital stock of \xc2\xa3838.3 million as of July 2014, supposed to guarantee the independence of the <i>Guardian</i> in perpetuity. In the first year, the paper made more losses than predicted, and in January 2016 the publishers announced, that <i>The Guardian</i> will cut 20 per cent of staff and costs within the next three years.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The newspaper is rare in calling for direct contributions "to deliver the independent journalism the world needs."<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Guardian Media Group\'s 2018 annual report (year ending 1 April 2018) indicated some significant changes occurring. Its digital (online) editions accounted for over 50% of group revenues by that time; the loss from news and media operations was \xc2\xa318.6 million, 52% lower than during the prior year (2017: \xc2\xa338.9 million). The Group had cut costs by \xc2\xa319.1 million, partly by switching its print edition to the tabloid format. The Guardian Media Group\'s owner, the Scott Trust Endowment Fund, reported that its value at the time was \xc2\xa31.01 billion (2017: \xc2\xa31.03 billion).<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> In the following financial report (for the year 2018/2019), the group reported a profit (<a href="/wiki/EBITDA" class="mw-redirect" title="EBITDA">EBITDA</a>) of \xc2\xa30.8 million before exceptional items, thus breaking even in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id=".22Membership.22_subscription_scheme"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Membership&quot;_subscription_scheme">"Membership" subscription scheme</span></h3>\n<p>In 2014, <i>The Guardian</i> launched a membership scheme.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> The scheme aims to reduce the financial losses incurred by <i>The Guardian</i> without introducing a <a href="/wiki/Paywall" title="Paywall">paywall</a>, thus maintaining open access to the website. Website readers can pay a monthly subscription, with three tiers available.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> As of 2018 this approach was considered successful, having brought more than 1 million subscriptions or donations, with the paper hoping to break even by April 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-20181112_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-20181112-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation_funding">Foundation funding</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Guardian_Foundation_-_Senate_House_History_Day_2019.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/The_Guardian_Foundation_-_Senate_House_History_Day_2019.jpg/220px-The_Guardian_Foundation_-_Senate_House_History_Day_2019.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/The_Guardian_Foundation_-_Senate_House_History_Day_2019.jpg/330px-The_Guardian_Foundation_-_Senate_House_History_Day_2019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/The_Guardian_Foundation_-_Senate_House_History_Day_2019.jpg/440px-The_Guardian_Foundation_-_Senate_House_History_Day_2019.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Guardian_Foundation_-_Senate_House_History_Day_2019.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Guardian Foundation at the Senate House History Day, 2019.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2016, the company established a U.S.-based philanthropic arm to raise money from individuals and organizations including think tanks and corporate foundations.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> The grants are focused by the donors on particular issues. By the following year, the organization had raised $1&#160;million from the likes of <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Omidyar" title="Pierre Omidyar">Pierre Omidyar</a>\'s Humanity United, the <a href="/wiki/Skoll_Foundation" title="Skoll Foundation">Skoll Foundation</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Conrad_N._Hilton_Foundation" title="Conrad N. Hilton Foundation">Conrad N. Hilton Foundation</a> to finance reporting on topics including modern-day slavery and climate change. <i>The Guardian</i> has stated that it has secured $6&#160;million "in multi-year funding commitments" thus far.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The new project developed from funding relationships which the paper already had with the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Foundation" title="Ford Foundation">Ford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Foundation" title="Rockefeller Foundation">Rockefeller</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bill_%26_Melinda_Gates_Foundation" title="Bill &amp; Melinda Gates Foundation">Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Gates had given the organization $5 million<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> for its Global Development webpage.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of March 2020, the journal claims to be "the first major global news organisation to institute an outright ban on taking money from companies that extract fossil fuels."<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_stance_and_editorial_opinion">Political stance and editorial opinion</span></h2>\n<p>Founded by textile traders and merchants, in its early years <i>The Guardian</i> had a reputation as "an organ of the middle class",<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> or in the words of C. P. Scott\'s son Ted, "a paper that will remain bourgeois to the last".<sup id="cite_ref-Hunter2003_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hunter2003-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Associated at first with the <a href="/wiki/Little_Circle" title="Little Circle">Little Circle</a> and hence with <a href="/wiki/Classical_liberalism" title="Classical liberalism">classical liberalism</a> as expressed by the <a href="/wiki/Whigs_(British_political_party)" title="Whigs (British political party)">Whigs</a> and later by the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(UK)" title="Liberal Party (UK)">Liberal Party</a>, its political orientation underwent a decisive change after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, leading to a gradual alignment with <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Political_left" class="mw-redirect" title="Political left">political left</a> in general.\n</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Scott_Trust_Limited" title="Scott Trust Limited">Scott Trust</a></i> describes one of its "core purposes" to be "to secure the financial and editorial independence of the <i>Guardian</i> in perpetuity: as a quality national newspaper without party affiliation; remaining faithful to its liberal tradition".<sup id="cite_ref-GST1_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GST1-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Affiliation_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Affiliation-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> The paper\'s readership is generally on the mainstream left of British political opinion: a <a href="/wiki/MORI" class="mw-redirect" title="MORI">MORI</a> poll taken between April and June 2000 showed that 80 per cent of <i>Guardian</i> readers were Labour Party voters;<sup id="cite_ref-International_Socialism_2003_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-International_Socialism_2003-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> according to another MORI poll taken in 2005, 48 per cent of <i>Guardian</i> readers were Labour voters and 34 per cent <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrat</a> voters.<sup id="cite_ref-Ipsos_MORI_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ipsos_MORI-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The newspaper\'s reputation as a platform for <a href="/wiki/Social_liberalism" title="Social liberalism">liberal</a> opinions has led to the use of the epithets "<i>Guardian</i> reader" and "Guardianista" for people holding such views, or as a stereotype of such people as middle class, earnest and <a href="/wiki/Politically_correct" class="mw-redirect" title="Politically correct">politically correct</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-What_the_papers_say_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-What_the_papers_say-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although the paper is often considered to be "linked inextricably" to the Labour Party,<sup id="cite_ref-Affiliation_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Affiliation-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> three of <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> four leader writers joined the more centrist <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_(UK)" title="Social Democratic Party (UK)">Social Democratic Party</a> on its foundation in 1981. The paper was enthusiastic in its support for <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> in his successful bid to lead the Labour Party,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> and to be elected Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> On 19 January 2003, two months before the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>, an <i>Observer</i> Editorial said: "Military intervention in the Middle East holds many dangers. But if we want a lasting peace it may be the only option. [\xe2\x80\xa6] War with Iraq may yet not come, but, conscious of the potentially terrifying responsibility resting with the British Government, we find ourselves supporting the current commitment to a possible use of force."<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> But <i>The Guardian</i> opposed the war, along with the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mirror" title="Daily Mirror">Daily Mirror</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Then <i>Guardian</i> features editor Ian Katz asserted in 2004 that "it is no secret we are a centre-left newspaper".<sup id="cite_ref-undecidedvoters_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-undecidedvoters-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, <i>Guardian</i> columnist <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Ashley" title="Jackie Ashley">Jackie Ashley</a> said that editorial contributors were a mix of "right-of-centre <a href="/wiki/Libertarianism" title="Libertarianism">libertarians</a>, greens, Blairites, Brownites, Labourite but less enthusiastic Brownites, etc," and that the newspaper was "clearly left of centre and vaguely progressive". She also said that "you can be absolutely certain that come the next general election, <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> stance will not be dictated by the editor, still less any foreign proprietor (it helps that there isn\'t one) but will be the result of vigorous debate within the paper".<sup id="cite_ref-Guardianistas_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardianistas-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The paper\'s comment and opinion pages, though often written by centre-left contributors such as <a href="/wiki/Polly_Toynbee" title="Polly Toynbee">Polly Toynbee</a>, have allowed some space for right-of-centre voices such as <a href="/wiki/Max_Hastings" title="Max Hastings">Sir Max Hastings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Gove" title="Michael Gove">Michael Gove</a>. Since an editorial in 2000, <i>The Guardian</i> has favoured abolition of the British monarchy.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> "I write for the <i>Guardian</i>," said Max Hastings in 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> "because it is read by the new establishment," reflecting the paper\'s then-growing influence.\n</p><p>In the run-up to the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2010 United Kingdom general election">2010 general election</a>, following a meeting of the editorial staff,<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> the paper declared its support for the Liberal Democrats, due in particular, to the party\'s stance on <a href="/wiki/Electoral_reform" title="Electoral reform">electoral reform</a>. The paper suggested <a href="/wiki/Tactical_voting" title="Tactical voting">tactical voting</a> to prevent a Conservative victory, given Britain\'s <a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">first-past-the-post</a> electoral system.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/2015_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2015 United Kingdom general election">the 2015 election</a>, the paper switched its support to the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>. The paper argued that Britain needed a new direction and Labour "speaks with more urgency than its rivals on social justice, standing up to predatory capitalism, on investment for growth, on reforming and strengthening the public realm, Britain\'s place in Europe and international development".<sup id="cite_ref-lab2015_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lab2015-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Assistant Editor Michael White, in discussing media self-censorship in March 2011, says: "I have always sensed liberal, middle class ill-ease in going after stories about immigration, legal or otherwise, about welfare fraud or the less attractive tribal habits of the working class, which is more easily ignored altogether. Toffs, including royal ones, Christians, especially popes, governments of Israel, and US <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republicans</a> are more straightforward targets."<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In a 2013 interview for <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a>, <i>The Guardian\'s</i> Latin America correspondent <a href="/wiki/Rory_Carroll" title="Rory Carroll">Rory Carroll</a> stated that many editors at <i>The Guardian</i> believed and continue to believe that they should support <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Ch\xc3\xa1vez">Hugo Ch\xc3\xa1vez</a> "because he was a standard-bearer for the left".<sup id="cite_ref-NPR2013_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR2013-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2015_Labour_Party_leadership_election_(UK)" title="2015 Labour Party leadership election (UK)">2015 Labour Party leadership election</a>, <i>The Guardian</i> supported <a href="/wiki/Yvette_Cooper" title="Yvette Cooper">Yvette Cooper</a> and was critical of left-winger <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn" title="Jeremy Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a>, the successful candidate.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> These positions were criticised by the <i><a href="/wiki/Morning_Star_(British_newspaper)" title="Morning Star (British newspaper)">Morning Star</a></i>, which accused <i>The Guardian</i> of being conservative.<sup id="cite_ref-MS1_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MS1-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Although the majority of political columnists in <i>The Guardian</i> were against Corbyn winning, <a href="/wiki/Owen_Jones_(writer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Owen Jones (writer)">Owen Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seumas_Milne" title="Seumas Milne">Seumas Milne</a>, and <a href="/wiki/George_Monbiot" title="George Monbiot">George Monbiot</a> wrote supportive articles about him.\n</p><p>Despite this critical position, in the 2017 election <i>The Guardian</i> endorsed the Labour Party.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> In the 2019 European election <i>The Guardian</i> invited its readers to vote for pro-EU candidates, without endorsing specific parties.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Circulation_and_format">Circulation and format</span></h2>\n<p><i>The Guardian</i> had a certified average daily circulation of 204,222 copies in December 2012&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 a drop of 11.25 per cent in January 2012&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 as compared to sales of 547,465 for <i>The Daily Telegraph</i>, 396,041 for <i>The Times</i>, and 78,082 for <i>The Independent</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> In March 2013, its average daily circulation had fallen to 193,586, according to the Audit Bureau of Circulations.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Circulation has continued to decline and stood at 161,091 in December 2016, a decline of 2.98 per cent year-on-year.<sup id="cite_ref-circ_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-circ-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Publication_history">Publication history</span></h3>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GuardianNewsroom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/GuardianNewsroom.jpg/220px-GuardianNewsroom.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/GuardianNewsroom.jpg/330px-GuardianNewsroom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/GuardianNewsroom.jpg/440px-GuardianNewsroom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1760" data-file-height="1168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GuardianNewsroom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> Newsroom visitor centre and archive (No 60), with an old sign with the name <i>The Manchester Guardian</i></div></div></div>\n<p>The first edition was published on 5 May 1821,<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> at which time <i>The Guardian</i> was a weekly, published on Saturdays and costing 7<a href="/wiki/Penny_(British_pre-decimal_coin)" title="Penny (British pre-decimal coin)">d</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Stamp_duty" title="Stamp duty">stamp duty</a> on newspapers (4d per sheet) forced the price up so high that it was uneconomic to publish more frequently. When the stamp duty was cut in 1836, <i>The Guardian</i> added a Wednesday edition and with the abolition of the tax in 1855 it became a daily paper costing 2d.\n</p><p>In October 1952, the paper took the step of printing news on the front page, replacing the adverts that had hitherto filled that space. Then-editor A. P. Wadsworth wrote: "It is not a thing I like myself, but it seems to be accepted by all the newspaper pundits that it is preferable to be in fashion."<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the closure of the Anglican Church Newspaper, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian_(Anglican_newspaper)" title="The Guardian (Anglican newspaper)">The Guardian</a></i>, in 1951, the paper dropped "Manchester" from its title in 1959, becoming simply <i>The Guardian.</i><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> In 1964 it moved to London, losing some of its regional agenda but continuing to be heavily subsidised by sales of the more downmarket but more profitable <i>Manchester Evening News</i>. The financial position remained extremely poor into the 1970s; at one time it was in merger talks with <i>The Times</i>. The paper consolidated its centre-left stance during the 1970s and 1980s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sima_Wali_on_the_front_page_of_The_Guardian_newspaper_in_2001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Sima_Wali_on_the_front_page_of_The_Guardian_newspaper_in_2001.jpg/220px-Sima_Wali_on_the_front_page_of_The_Guardian_newspaper_in_2001.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/ba/Sima_Wali_on_the_front_page_of_The_Guardian_newspaper_in_2001.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="269" data-file-height="369" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sima_Wali_on_the_front_page_of_The_Guardian_newspaper_in_2001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Front page of <i>The Guardian</i> from 2001, showing the old design of the paper when in broadsheet format. This design was used from 1988 to 2005</div></div></div>\n<p>On 12 February 1988, <i>The Guardian</i> had a significant redesign; as well as improving the quality of its printers\' ink, it also changed its masthead to a juxtaposition of an <a href="/wiki/Italic_type" title="Italic type">italic</a> <a href="/wiki/Garamond" title="Garamond">Garamond</a> "<i>The</i>", with a bold <a href="/wiki/Helvetica" title="Helvetica">Helvetica</a> "Guardian", that remained in use until the 2005 redesign.\n</p><p>In 1992, <i>The Guardian</i> relaunched its features section as <i>G2</i>, a tabloid-format supplement. This innovation was widely copied by the other "quality" broadsheets and ultimately led to the rise of "compact" papers and <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> move to the <a href="/wiki/Berliner_(format)" title="Berliner (format)">Berliner format</a>. In 1993 the paper declined to participate in the broadsheet <a href="/wiki/Price_war" title="Price war">price war</a> started by <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Murdoch" title="Rupert Murdoch">Rupert Murdoch</a>\'s <i>The Times</i>. In June 1993, <i>The Guardian</i> bought <i>The Observer</i> from <a href="/wiki/Lonrho" title="Lonrho">Lonrho</a>, thus gaining a serious <a href="/wiki/Sunday_editions" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunday editions">Sunday sister newspaper</a> with similar political views.\n</p><p>Its international weekly edition is now titled <i>The Guardian Weekly</i>, though it retained the title <i>Manchester Guardian Weekly</i> for some years after the home edition had moved to London. It includes sections from a number of other internationally significant newspapers of a somewhat left-of-centre inclination, including <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>. <i>The Guardian Weekly</i> was also linked to a website for expatriates, <i>Guardian Abroad</i>, which was launched in 2007 but had been taken offline by 2012.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moving_to_the_Berliner_paper_format">Moving to the Berliner paper format</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Guardian_6._6._14.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/ca/The_Guardian_6._6._14.jpg/220px-The_Guardian_6._6._14.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/ca/The_Guardian_6._6._14.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="257" data-file-height="387" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Guardian_6._6._14.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Front page of 6 June 2014 edition in the Berliner format.</div></div></div>\n<p><i>The Guardian</i> is printed in full colour,<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> and was the first newspaper in the UK to use the <a href="/wiki/Berliner_(format)" title="Berliner (format)">Berliner</a> format for its main section, while producing sections and supplements in a range of page sizes including tabloid, approximately A4, and pocket-size (approximately A5).\n</p><p>In 2004, <i>The Guardian</i> announced plans to change to a Berliner or "midi" format,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> similar to that used by <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Tageszeitung" title="Die Tageszeitung">Die Tageszeitung</a></i> in Germany, <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a></i> in France and many other European papers. At 470\xc3\x97315&#160;mm, this is slightly larger than a traditional <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_(newspaper_format)" title="Tabloid (newspaper format)">tabloid</a>. Planned for the autumn of 2005, this change followed moves by <i>The Independent</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> to start publishing in tabloid (or compact) format. On Thursday, 1 September 2005, <i>The Guardian</i> announced that it would launch the new format on Monday 12 September 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Sister Sunday newspaper <i>The Observer</i> also changed to this new format on 8 January 2006.\n</p><p>The format switch was accompanied by a comprehensive redesign of the paper\'s look. On Friday, 9 September 2005, the newspaper unveiled its newly designed front page, which d\xc3\xa9buted on Monday 12 September 2005. Designed by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Porter_(designer)" title="Mark Porter (designer)">Mark Porter</a>, the new look includes a new <a href="/wiki/Masthead_(British_publishing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Masthead (British publishing)">masthead</a> for the newspaper, its first since 1988. A typeface family designed by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Barnes_(designer)" title="Paul Barnes (designer)">Paul Barnes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christian_Schwartz" title="Christian Schwartz">Christian Schwartz</a> was created for the new design. With just over 200 fonts, it was described as "one of the most ambitious custom type programs ever commissioned by a newspaper".<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fontshop2006_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fontshop2006-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Among the fonts is <a href="/wiki/Guardian_Egyptian" title="Guardian Egyptian">Guardian Egyptian</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Slab_serif" title="Slab serif">slab serif</a> that is used in various weights for both text and headlines, and is central to the redesign.\n</p><p>The switch cost <i>Guardian Newspapers</i> \xc2\xa380&#160;million and involved setting up new printing presses in east London and Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> This switch was necessary because, before <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> move, no printing presses in Britain could produce newspapers in the Berliner format. There were additional complications, as one of the paper\'s presses was part-owned by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">Telegraph Newspapers</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="The Daily Express">Express Newspapers</a></i>, contracted to use the plant until 2009. Another press was shared with the <i>Guardian Media Group\'s</i> north-western tabloid local papers, which did not wish to switch to the Berliner format.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span></h4>\n<p>The new format was generally well received by <i>Guardian</i> readers, who were encouraged to provide feedback on the changes. The only controversy was over the dropping of the <i><a href="/wiki/Doonesbury" title="Doonesbury">Doonesbury</a></i> cartoon strip. The paper reported thousands of calls and emails complaining about its loss; within 24 hours the decision was reversed and the strip was reinstated the following week. <i>G2</i> supplement editor Ian Katz, who was responsible for dropping it, apologised in the editors\' blog saying, "I\'m sorry, once again, that I made you\xe2\x80\x94and the hundreds of fellow fans who have called our helpline or mailed our comments\' address\xe2\x80\x94so cross."<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> However, some readers were dissatisfied as the earlier deadline needed for the all-colour sports section meant coverage of late-finishing evening football matches became less satisfactory in the editions supplied to some parts of the country.\n</p><p>The investment was rewarded with a circulation rise. In December 2005, the average daily sale stood at 380,693, nearly 6 per cent higher than the figure for December 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> (However, as of December 2012, circulation had dropped to 204,222.)<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, the US-based <a href="/wiki/Society_for_News_Design" title="Society for News Design">Society for News Design</a> chose <i>The Guardian</i> and Polish daily <i><a href="/wiki/Rzeczpospolita_(newspaper)" title="Rzeczpospolita (newspaper)">Rzeczpospolita</a></i> as the world\'s best-designed newspapers\xe2\x80\x94from among 389 entries from 44 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tabloid_format_since_2018">Tabloid format since 2018</span></h3>\n<p>In June 2017, <a href="/wiki/Guardian_Media_Group" title="Guardian Media Group">Guardian Media Group</a> (GMG) announced that <i>The Guardian</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i> would relaunch in <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_(newspaper_format)" title="Tabloid (newspaper format)">tabloid format</a> from early 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-tabloid_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tabloid-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Guardian</i> confirmed the launch date for the new format to be 15 January 2018. GMG also signed a contract with <i><a href="/wiki/Trinity_Mirror" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinity Mirror">Trinity Mirror</a></i> \xe2\x80\x93 the publisher of the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mirror" title="Daily Mirror">Daily Mirror</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Mirror" title="Sunday Mirror">Sunday Mirror</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_People" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunday People">Sunday People</a></i> \xe2\x80\x93 to <a href="/wiki/Outsourcing" title="Outsourcing">outsource</a> printing of <i>The Guardian</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The format change is intended to help cut costs as it allows the paper to be printed by a wider array of presses, and outsourcing the printing to presses owned by Trinity Mirror is expected to save millions of pounds annually.  The move is part of a three-year plan that includes cutting 300 jobs in an attempt to reduce losses and break even by 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-tabloid_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tabloid-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> The paper and ink are the same as previously and the font size is fractionally larger.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An assessment of the response from readers in late April 2018 indicated that the new format had led to an increased number of subscriptions. The editors were working on changing aspects that had caused complaints from readers.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2018, the masthead of the new tabloid format was adjusted to a dark blue.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_media">Online media</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/TheGuardian.com" title="TheGuardian.com">TheGuardian.com</a></div>\n<p><i>The Guardian</i> and its Sunday sibling <i>The Observer</i> publish all their news online, with free access both to current news and an archive of three million stories. A third of the site\'s hits are for items over a month old.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> As of May 2013, it was the most popular UK newspaper website with 8.2 million unique visitors per month, just ahead of <i><a href="/wiki/Mail_Online" class="mw-redirect" title="Mail Online">Mail Online</a></i> with 7.6 million unique monthly visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-journalism553108_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journalism553108-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> In April 2011, <a href="/wiki/Haymarket_Media_Group" title="Haymarket Media Group">MediaWeek</a> reported that <i>The Guardian</i> was the fifth most popular newspaper site in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Journalists use an analytics tool called Ophan, built entire in-house, to measure website data around stories and audience.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>The Guardian</i> launched an <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">mobile application</a> for its content in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> app followed in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, the newspaper announced its apps and mobile website would be redesigned to coincide with its relaunch as a tabloid.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Comment_is_Free" class="mw-redirect" title="Comment is Free">Comment is Free</a> section features columns by the paper\'s journalists and regular commentators, as well as articles from guest writers, including readers\' comments and responses below. The section includes all the opinion pieces published in the paper itself, as well as many others that only appear online. Censorship is exercised by Moderators who can ban posts&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 with no right of appeal&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 by those who they feel have overstepped the mark. <i>The Guardian</i> has taken what they call a very "open" stance in delivering news, and have launched an open platform for their content. This allows external developers to easily use <i>Guardian</i> content in external applications, and even to feed third-party content back into the <i>Guardian</i> network.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Guardian</i> also had a number of talkboards that were noted for their mix of political discussion and whimsy until they were closed on Friday, 25 February 2011 after they had settled a libel action brought after months of harassment of a conservative party activist.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> They were spoofed in <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> own regular humorous Chatroom column in <i>G2</i>. The spoof column purported to be excerpts from a chatroom on permachat.co.uk, a real URL that pointed to <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> talkboards.\n</p><p>In August 2013, a webshow titled <i>Thinkfluencer</i><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> was launched by Guardian Multimedia in association with <a href="/wiki/Arte" title="Arte">Arte</a>.\n</p><p>In 2004 the paper also launched a dating website, Guardian Soulmates;<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> this is to close at the end of June 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Podcasts">Podcasts</span></h3>\n<p>The paper entered <a href="/wiki/Podcasting" class="mw-redirect" title="Podcasting">podcasting</a> in 2005 with a twelve-part weekly <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">podcast</a> series by <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Gervais" title="Ricky Gervais">Ricky Gervais</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> In January 2006, Gervais\' show topped the <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> podcast chart having been downloaded by two million listeners worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> and was scheduled to be listed in the 2007 <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinness Book of Records">Guinness Book of Records</a></i> as the most downloaded podcast.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>The Guardian</i> now offers several regular podcasts made by its journalists. One of the most prominent is <i>Today in Focus</i>, a daily news podcast hosted by <a href="/wiki/Anushka_Asthana" title="Anushka Asthana">Anushka Asthana</a> and launched on 1 November 2018. It was an immediate success<sup id="cite_ref-BMA_20190522_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BMA_20190522-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> and became one of the UK\'s most-downloaded podcasts.<sup id="cite_ref-BMA_20190522_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BMA_20190522-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="GuardianFilms">GuardianFilms</span></h2>\n<p>In 2003, <i>The Guardian</i> started the film production company GuardianFilms, headed by journalist Maggie O\'Kane. Much of the company\'s output is documentary made for television\xe2\x80\x93 and it has included <a href="/wiki/Salam_Pax" title="Salam Pax">Salam Pax</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Baghdad_Blogger" class="mw-redirect" title="Baghdad Blogger">Baghdad Blogger</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two" title="BBC Two">BBC Two</a>\'s daily flagship <i><a href="/wiki/Newsnight" title="Newsnight">Newsnight</a></i>, some of which have been shown in compilations by <i><a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> International</i>, <i>Sex on the Streets</i> and <i>Spiked</i>, both made for the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a> television.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>GuardianFilms has received several broadcasting awards. In addition to two Amnesty International Media Awards in 2004 and 2005, <i>The Baghdad Blogger: Salam Pax</i> won a Royal Television Society Award in 2005. <i>Baghdad: A Doctor\'s Story</i> won an Emmy Award for Best International Current Affairs film in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Smith_(photojournalist_and_filmmaker)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sean Smith (photojournalist and filmmaker)">photojournalist Sean Smith\'s</a> <i>Inside the Surge</i> won the Royal Television Society award for best international news film&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 the first time a newspaper has won such an award.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> The same year, <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> <a href="/wiki/Katine" title="Katine">Katine</a> website was awarded for its outstanding new media output at the One World Media awards. Again in 2008, GuardianFilms\' undercover video report revealing vote rigging by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">Robert Mugabe</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/ZANU%E2%80%93PF" title="ZANU\xe2\x80\x93PF">ZANU\xe2\x80\x93PF</a> party during the 2007 Zimbabwe election won best news programme of the year at the Broadcast Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_228-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References_in_popular_culture">References in popular culture</span></h2>\n<p>The paper\'s nickname <i>The Grauniad</i> (sometimes abbreviated as "Graun") originated with the satirical magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Private_Eye_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Private Eye (magazine)">Private Eye</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Anagram" title="Anagram">anagram</a> played on <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s early reputation for frequent <a href="/wiki/Typographical_error" title="Typographical error">typographical errors</a>, including misspelling its own name as <i>The Gaurdian</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bernhard_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bernhard-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first issue of the newspaper contained a number of errors, including a notification that there would soon be some goods sold at <i>atction</i> instead of <i>auction</i>. Fewer typographical errors are seen in the paper since the end of <a href="/wiki/Hot_metal_typesetting" title="Hot metal typesetting">hot-metal typesetting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> One <i>Guardian</i> writer, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Devlin" title="Keith Devlin">Keith Devlin</a>, suggested that the high number of observed misprints was due more to the quality of the readership than the misprints\' greater frequency.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> The fact that the newspaper was printed in Manchester until 1961 and the early, more error-prone, prints were sent to London by train may have contributed to this image as well.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bernhard_233-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bernhard-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/John_Cole_(journalist)" title="John Cole (journalist)">John Cole</a> was appointed news editor by <a href="/wiki/Alastair_Hetherington" title="Alastair Hetherington">Alastair Hetherington</a> in 1963, he sharpened the paper\'s comparatively "amateurish" setup.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_obit_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_obit-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Employees of The Guardian and sister paper The Observer have been depicted in the films <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fifth_Estate_(film)" title="The Fifth Estate (film)">The Fifth Estate</a></i> (2013), <i><a href="/wiki/Snowden_(film)" title="Snowden (film)">Snowden</a></i> (2016) and <i><a href="/wiki/Official_Secrets_(film)" title="Official Secrets (film)">Official Secrets</a></i> (2019), while <a href="/wiki/Paddy_Considine" title="Paddy Considine">Paddy Considine</a> played a fictional Guardian journalist in the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bourne_Ultimatum_(film)" title="The Bourne Ultimatum (film)">The Bourne Ultimatum</a></i> (2007).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Received">Received</span></h3>\n<p><i>The Guardian</i> has been awarded the National Newspaper of the Year in 1998, 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-gazetteroll_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gazetteroll-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> 2010<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian06042011_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian06042011-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> and 2013<sup id="cite_ref-award_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-award-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> by the <a href="/wiki/British_Press_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="British Press Awards">British Press Awards</a>, and Front Page of the Year in 2002 ("A declaration of war", 12 September 2001).<sup id="cite_ref-gazetteroll_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gazetteroll-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> It was also co-winner of the World\'s Best-designed Newspaper as awarded by the <a href="/wiki/Society_for_News_Design" title="Society for News Design">Society for News Design</a> (2005, 2007, 2013, 2014).<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>Guardian</i> journalists have won a range of British Press Awards, including:<sup id="cite_ref-gazetteroll_238-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gazetteroll-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Reporter of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Nick_Davies" title="Nick Davies">Nick Davies</a>, 2000;<sup id="cite_ref-British_Press_Awards:_Past_winners_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-British_Press_Awards:_Past_winners-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Lewis_(journalist)" title="Paul Lewis (journalist)">Paul Lewis</a>, 2010;<sup id="cite_ref-gazetteroll2_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gazetteroll2-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> Rob Evans &amp; Paul Lewis, 2014);<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Foreign Reporter of the Year (<a href="/wiki/James_Meek_(author)" title="James Meek (author)">James Meek</a>, 2004;<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ghaith_Abdul-Ahad" title="Ghaith Abdul-Ahad">Ghaith Abdul-Ahad</a>, 2008);<sup id="cite_ref-pressg08_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pressg08-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Scoop of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Milly_Dowler" class="mw-redirect" title="Milly Dowler">Milly Dowler</a> phone hacked, 2012)<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Young Journalist of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Emma_Brockes" title="Emma Brockes">Emma Brockes</a>, 2001;<sup id="cite_ref-BCouncil_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BCouncil-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Kingsley_(journalist)" title="Patrick Kingsley (journalist)">Patrick Kingsley</a>, 2013);<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Columnist of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Polly_Toynbee" title="Polly Toynbee">Polly Toynbee</a>, 2007;<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Brooker" title="Charlie Brooker">Charlie Brooker</a>, 2009);<sup id="cite_ref-pressgazette1_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pressgazette1-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Critic of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Marina_O%27Loughlin" title="Marina O&#39;Loughlin">Marina O\'Loughlin</a>, 2015);<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Feature Writer of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Emma_Brockes" title="Emma Brockes">Emma Brockes</a>, 2002;<sup id="cite_ref-BCouncil_248-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BCouncil-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tanya_Gold" title="Tanya Gold">Tanya Gold</a>, 2009;<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian06042011-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Cartoonist of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Steve_Bell_(cartoonist)" title="Steve Bell (cartoonist)">Steve Bell</a>, 2003);<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Political Journalist of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Patrick_Wintour" title="Patrick Wintour">Patrick Wintour</a>, 2006; <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Sparrow" title="Andrew Sparrow">Andrew Sparrow</a>, 2010);<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian06042011_239-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian06042011-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Science &amp; Health Journalist of the Year (Sarah Boseley, 2016);<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Business &amp; Finance Journalist of the Year (Ian Griffiths, 2005;<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> Simon Goodley, 2014);<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Interviewer of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Decca_Aitkenhead" title="Decca Aitkenhead">Decca Aitkenhead</a>, 2008);<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Sports Reporter of the Year (David Lacey, 2002);<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Sports Photographer of the Year (Tom Jenkins, 2003, 2005, 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> 2015);<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Website of the Year (guardian.com/uk, 1999, 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> 2020);<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Digital Journalist of the Year (Dan Milmo, 2001;<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> Sean Smith, 2008;<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> Dave Hill, 2009)<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Supplement of the Year (<i>Guardian\'s Guides to...</i>, 2007;<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> <i>Weekend Magazine</i>, 2015)<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Special Supplement of the Year (<i>World Cup 2010 Guide</i>, 2010)<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian06042011_239-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian06042011-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>Other awards include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bevins_Prize" title="Bevins Prize">Bevins Prize</a> for investigative journalism (<a href="/wiki/Paul_Lewis_(journalist)" title="Paul Lewis (journalist)">Paul Lewis</a>, 2010);<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Martha_Gellhorn_Prize_for_Journalism" title="Martha Gellhorn Prize for Journalism">Martha Gellhorn Prize for Journalism</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nick_Davies" title="Nick Davies">Nick Davies</a>, 1999; <a href="/wiki/Chris_McGreal" title="Chris McGreal">Chris McGreal</a>, 2003; <a href="/wiki/Ghaith_Abdul-Ahad" title="Ghaith Abdul-Ahad">Ghaith Abdul-Ahad</a>, 2005;<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ian_Cobain" title="Ian Cobain">Ian Cobain</a>, 2009).<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>The <i>Guardian, Observer</i> and its journalists have also won numerous accolades at the <a href="/wiki/British_Sports_Journalism_Awards" title="British Sports Journalism Awards">British Sports Journalism Awards</a>:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Sports Writer of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Daniel_Taylor_(journalist)" title="Daniel Taylor (journalist)">Daniel Taylor</a>, 2017)<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Sports News Reporter of the Year (<a href="/wiki/David_Conn" title="David Conn">David Conn</a>, 2009, 2014)<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Football Journalist of the Year (Daniel Taylor, 2015, 2016, 2017)<sup id="cite_ref-:0_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Sports Interviewer of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Donald_McRae_(author)" title="Donald McRae (author)">Donald McRae</a>, 2009, 2011)<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Diarist of the Year (David Hills, 2009)<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Sports Feature Writer of the Year (Donald McRae, 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> 2018)<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Specialist Correspondent of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Sean_Ingle" title="Sean Ingle">Sean Ingle</a>, 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> 2017)<sup id="cite_ref-:2_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Scoop of the Year (Daniel Taylor 2016;<sup id="cite_ref-:0_277-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Martha_Kelner" title="Martha Kelner">Martha Kelner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sean_Ingle" title="Sean Ingle">Sean Ingle</a>, 2017)<sup id="cite_ref-:2_283-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Sports Newspaper of the Year (2017)<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Sports Website of the Year (2014, 2015, 2016, 2017)<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Sports Journalists\' Association Sports Portfolio of the Year (Tom Jenkins, 2011)<sup id="cite_ref-:1_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>The <i>guardian.co.uk</i> website won the Best Newspaper category three years running in 2005, 2006 and 2007 <a href="/wiki/Webby_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Webby Award">Webby Awards</a>, beating (in 2005) <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, <i>The Washington Post</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> It has been the winner for six years in a row of the British Press Awards for Best Electronic Daily Newspaper.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> The site won an <i><a href="/wiki/Editor_%26_Publisher" title="Editor &amp; Publisher">Eppy</a></i> award from the US-based magazine <i>Editor &amp; Publisher</i> in 2000 for the best-designed newspaper online service.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, the newspaper was ranked first in a study on transparency that analysed 25 mainstream English-language media vehicles, which was conducted by the International Center for Media and the Public Agenda of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park" title="University of Maryland, College Park">University of Maryland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> It scored 3.8 out of a possible 4.0.\n</p><p><i>The Guardian</i> and <i>The Washington Post</i> shared the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_Public_Service" title="Pulitzer Prize for Public Service">Pulitzer Prize for public service reporting</a> for their coverage of the NSA\'s and GCHQ\'s worldwide electronic surveillance program and the document leaks by whistleblower Edward Snowden.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Given">Given</span></h3>\n<p><i>The Guardian</i> is the sponsor of two major literary awards: The <i><a href="/wiki/Guardian_First_Book_Award" title="Guardian First Book Award">Guardian First Book Award</a></i>, established in 1999 as a successor to the <i><a href="/wiki/Guardian_Fiction_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Guardian Fiction Award">Guardian Fiction Award</a></i>, which had run since 1965, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Guardian_Children%27s_Fiction_Prize" title="Guardian Children&#39;s Fiction Prize">Guardian Children\'s Fiction Prize</a></i>, founded in 1967. In recent years the newspaper has also sponsored the <a href="/wiki/Hay_Festival" title="Hay Festival">Hay Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hay-on-Wye" title="Hay-on-Wye">Hay-on-Wye</a>.\n</p><p>The annual <a href="/wiki/Guardian_Student_Media_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Guardian Student Media Awards">Guardian Student Media Awards</a>, founded in 1999, recognise excellence in journalism and design of British university and college <a href="/wiki/Student_newspapers" class="mw-redirect" title="Student newspapers">student newspapers</a>, magazines and websites.\n</p><p>In memory of <a href="/wiki/Paul_Foot_(journalist)" title="Paul Foot (journalist)">Paul Foot</a>, who died in 2004, <i>The Guardian</i> and <i>Private Eye</i> jointly set up the <a href="/wiki/Paul_Foot_Award" title="Paul Foot Award">Paul Foot Award</a>, with an annual \xc2\xa310,000 prize fund, for investigative or campaigning journalism.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The newspaper produces <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian_100_Best_Footballers_In_The_World" class="mw-redirect" title="The Guardian 100 Best Footballers In The World"><i>The Guardian</i> 100 Best Footballers In The World</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> Since 2018 it has also co-produced the female equivalent, <a href="/wiki/The_100_Best_Female_Footballers_In_The_World" title="The 100 Best Female Footballers In The World">The 100 Best Female Footballers In The World</a>.\n</p><p>In 2016, <i>The Guardian</i> began awarding an annual <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="The Guardian Footballer of the Year">Footballer of the Year</a> award, given to a footballer regardless of gender "who has done something truly remarkable, whether by overcoming adversity, helping others or setting a sporting example by acting with exceptional honesty."<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Best_books_lists">Best books lists</span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian%27s_100_Best_Novels_Written_in_English" title="The Guardian&#39;s 100 Best Novels Written in English"><i>The Guardian\'</i>s 100 best novels</a> is a list of the best English-language novels as selected by <a href="/wiki/Robert_McCrum" title="Robert McCrum">Robert McCrum</a>.</li>\n<li><i>The Guardian\'</i>s 100 greatest non-fiction book list has come out in 2011<sup id="cite_ref-100_Best_Nonfiction_2011_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100_Best_Nonfiction_2011-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> and in 2017, as selected by Robert McCrum.<sup id="cite_ref-100_Best_Nonfiction_2017_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100_Best_Nonfiction_2017-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Editors">Editors</span></h2>\n<table class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> first photographer, July 1908)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eamonn_McCabe" title="Eamonn McCabe">Eamonn McCabe</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sean_Smith_(photojournalist_and_filmmaker)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sean Smith (photojournalist and filmmaker)">Sean Smith</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span id="Guardian_News_.26_Media_archive"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Guardian_News_&amp;_Media_archive">Guardian News &amp; Media archive</span></h2>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><i>The Guardian</i> and its sister newspaper <i>The Observer</i> opened The Newsroom, an archive and visitor centre in London, in 2002. The centre preserved and promoted the histories and values of the newspapers through its archive, educational programmes and exhibitions. The Newsroom\'s activities were all transferred to <a href="/wiki/Kings_Place" title="Kings Place">Kings Place</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-test_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-test-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> Now known as the Guardian News &amp; Media archive, the archive preserves and promotes the histories and values of <i>The Guardian</i> and <i>The Observer</i> newspapers by collecting and making accessible material that provides an accurate and comprehensive history of the papers. The archive holds official records of <i>The Guardian</i> and <i>The Observer</i>, and also seeks to acquire material from individuals who have been associated with the papers. As well as corporate records, the archive holds correspondence, diaries, notebooks, original cartoons and photographs belonging to staff of the papers.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> This material may be consulted by members of the public by prior appointment. An extensive <i>Manchester Guardian</i> archive also exists at the University of Manchester\'s John Rylands University Library, and there is a collaboration programme between the two archives. Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a> has a large archive of <i>The Manchester Guardian</i> available in its British Library Newspapers collection, in online, hard copy, microform, and CD-ROM formats.\n</p><p>In November 2007, <i>The Guardian</i> and <i>The Observer</i> made their archives available over the internet via DigitalArchive. The current extent of the archives available are 1821 to 2000 for <i>The Guardian</i> and 1791 to 2000 for <i>The Observer</i>: these archives will eventually run up to 2003.\n</p><p>The Newsroom\'s other components were also transferred to Kings Place in 2008. <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> Education Centre provides a range of educational programmes for students and adults. <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> exhibition space was also moved to Kings Place, and has a rolling programme of exhibitions that investigate and reflect upon aspects of news and newspapers and the role of journalism. This programme often draws on the archive collections held in the GNM Archive.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<ul><li><a
